# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Key Findings

I've identified **22 Java source files** that implement the core consumer offset management system in Apache Kafka, organized into these main categories:

### 1. **OffsetAndMetadata Storage** (2 implementations)
- Client-side: Stores offset and metadata with leader epoch support
- Coordinator-side: Stores server-side offset metadata with commit timestamps and expiration tracking

### 2. **GroupCoordinator Components** (3 key files)
- `GroupCoordinator.java`: Interface defining offset operations
- `GroupCoordinatorService.java`: Main implementation orchestrating offset management
- `GroupCoordinatorShard.java`: Handles offset operations per partition

### 3. **Offset Management Core** (3 key files)
- `OffsetMetadataManager.java`: Central manager for offset commit/fetch/delete/expiration
- `OffsetExpirationCondition.java` & `OffsetExpirationConditionImpl.java`: Expiration policy framework

### 4. **Request/Response Handling** (4 files)
- OffsetCommit and OffsetFetch request/response classes for client-server communication

### 5. **Client-Side Coordination** (3 files)
- `CommitRequestManager.java`: Manages client offset commit requests
- `ConsumerCoordinator.java`: High-level consumer coordination
- `OffsetCommitCallbackInvoker.java`: Callback management

### 6. **Request Processing** 
- `KafkaApis.scala`: Server-side handler routing offset requests to the coordinator

\\n67:     <p>On compaction, we preserve the first and last offset/sequence numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\\n68:     producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, for example, then after a partition leader failure, the producer might see an OutOfSequence error. The base sequence number must\\n69:     be preserved for duplicate checking (the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer). As a result,\\n70:     it is possible to have empty batches in the log when all the records in the batch are cleaned but batch is still retained in order to preserve a producer's last sequence number. One oddity here is that the baseTimestamp\\n71:     field is not preserved during compaction, so it will change if the first record in the batch is compacted away.</p>\\n72: \\n73: ...             "content": "66: \n67:     <p>On compaction, we preserve the first and last offset/sequence numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\n68:     producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, for example, then after a partition leader failure, the producer might see an OutOfSequence error. The base sequence number must\n69:     be preserved for duplicate checking (the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer). As a result,\n70:     it is possible to have empty batches in the log when all the records in the batch are cleaned but batch is still retained in order to preserve a producer's last sequence number. One oddity here is that the baseTimestamp\n71:     field is not preserved during compaction, so it will change if the first record in the batch is compacted away.</p>\n72: \n73: ... GroupCoordinator Interface and Implementation\\nThe core coordinator system:\\n- **GroupCoordinator.java** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/): Defines the interface for offset commit, fetch, and delete operations.\\n- **GroupCoordinatorService.java**: Implements the GroupCoordinator interface, orchestrating offset management across multiple coordinator shards.\\n- **GroupCoordinatorShard.java**: Handles offset operations for a specific partition of the group metadata.\\n\\n### 3. Offset Commit Handler\\nThe offset commit flow:\\n1. Client sends OffsetCommitRequest (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/OffsetCommitRequest.java)\\n2. KafkaApis.handleOffsetCommitRequest (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaApis.scala) routes to GroupCoordinator.commitOffsets()\\n3. GroupCoordinatorService.commitOffsets() processes the request\\n4. GroupCoordinatorShard.commitOffsets() persists offsets via OffsetMetadataManager\\n5. OffsetAndMetadata objects are stored in __consumer_offsets topic for durability and log compaction\\n\\nThe CommitRequestManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) on the client side manages offset commit requests with retries and batching.\\n\\n### 4. OffsetMetadataManager.fetchOffsets() retrieves from in-memory cache or compacted topic\\n5. OffsetMetadataManager.fetchOffsets() retrieves from in-memory cache or compacted topic\\n5. Response sent via OffsetFetchResponse\\n\\nThe CommitRequestManager.fetchOffsets() manages client-side offset fetch requests with support for committed offsets lookup.\\n\\n### 5. Offset Expiry and Compaction Logic\\nOffset expiration is managed through:\\n- **OffsetExpirationCondition.java** and **OffsetExpirationConditionImpl.java**: Define expiration policies based on commit timestamps.\\n- **Group implementations** (ClassicGroup, ConsumerGroup, StreamsGroup) provide offsetExpirationCondition() to determine when offsets should expire.\\n- **OffsetMetadataManager.removeExpiredOffsets()**: Removes expired offsets and produces tombstone records to the __consumer_offsets topic for log compaction.\\n\\nEach group type can customize expiration logic:\\n- ClassicGroup: Uses commit timestamp for expiration\\n- ConsumerGroup: Uses commit timestamp for expiration\\n- StreamsGroup: Uses commit timestamp for expiration\\n- ShareGroup: Does not support offset expiration\\n\\nOffsets are deleted via:\\n- **GroupCoordinator.deleteOffsets()**: Explicit deletion via admin API\\n- **OffsetMetadataManager.deleteOffsets()**: Produces delete tombstones for log compaction\\n\\nThe __consumer_offsets topic uses log compaction cleanup policy to maintain only the latest offset commit per group+topic+partition combination, automatically cleaning up stale offset records.\\n\\n### 6. Supporting Components\\n- **OffsetCommitCallbackInvoker** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetCommitCallbackInvoker.java): Invokes callbacks after offset commits complete\\n- **OffsetCommitMetricsManager** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/metrics/OffsetCommitMetricsManager.java): Tracks offset commit metrics\\n- **ConsumerCoordinator** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java): High-level consumer coordination including offset management\\n\\nThe architecture ensures reliable, durable offset storage with automatic cleanup and expiration of stale offsets through Kafka's log compaction mechanism.\"\n}\n",
